msg:Among the Shangri-La hotels I have stayed in in China, Yangzhou Station is the most disappointing.

Facilities: The hardware of the old hotel is indeed not very promising. The stereotype that there is no socket in the bathroom does exist.

Environment: The hotel is located in a development zone under development. Mingyue Lake is about the same as a pond. During the stay, it coincided with the dredging construction, so there is really no lake view; opposite the hotel is the museum area, you can visit the museum and art gallery nearby, and the quiet environment is still ok.

Service: Adhering to the unmatched service level in Jiangsu Province, Yangzhou Shangri-La does not give people unexpected surprises at all. The team chatting and complaining around you when checking in, the waiters who are always absent in the executive lounge, the executive lounge wanna-be with inferior purchased biscuits and cakes, and the catering content and service level (including breakfast and Xiang Palace) that make you doubt the level of Shangri-La, it is destined to be a one-time trip.

If it were not for the Xiangjia brand, I would probably ask Ctrip for help to check out when checking in.

ps Xiangjia's mini zoo only had three little rabbits left in Yangzhou, which was quite lonely.

On the day of check-in, I called the hotel and hoped to arrange a room with a better view. Ms. Wang Qian, guest director of the reservation depar**ent, immediately agreed. When she learned that the next day was my husband and I's wedding anniversary, she even offered to help us make a simple decoration of the room and arranged for the hotel's pastry depar**ent to help make a freshly made cake to express her blessing. To tell the truth: This is really very thoughtful.
When we were visiting Slender West Lake, Miss Wang Qian called us to tell us that the room had been decorated and we could check in early. And that night when we went for a night tour of Slender West Lake, she called us again and told us: the cake had been made and could be delivered to the room. All these arrangements made us feel at home.
Let‚Äôs talk about hotel facilities and room layout. Yangzhou Shangri-La was renovated in 2019. Whether it is the hotel lobby, restaurants, or guest rooms, there is an antique charm everywhere, low-key yet luxurious, and a clever combination of ancient Chinese style and fashionable a**osphere. Really my favorite style.
The room arranged by Xiao Wang faces the private garden of the hotel. The lake is pleasing to the eye and echoes the Yangzhou Opera House in the distance. There are no tall buildings on the side, so it has good privacy. It is really pleasant to sit by the window and watch the night view or bask in the sun. The bedding is also good, and the curtains are basically light-proof. I have poor sleep quality, but I really slept well this night.
I read a lot of reviews saying that Shang Palace‚Äôs morning tea is great, so I wanted to give it a try. But the room rate includes two breakfasts, and I would be reluctant to give it up, so I went to enjoy the hotel's breakfast. Facts have proved that this decision was correct. The variety of meals is very rich: there are canned tuna and cheese powder in the salad bar. This is the first time I have seen it in many five-star hotels when I have traveled extensively. The little wontons that are freshly made in the kitchen are chubby. After the chef cooks them, he puts a little lard in the soup. They taste really good. There are a lot of fillings for various kinds of steamed buns, and I think they taste better than the ones in Yechun.
The hotel's employees have a strong sense of service and will proactively greet guests and respond to requests. When we were taking photos in the back garden, several repairmen were soft-spoken and gentle while working. Restaurant waiters will coax babies who can't eat well. Many details made me feel that Shangri-La's training of employees is quite good.
Next time I come to Yangzhou, Shangri-La will be my first choice!
